Current Affairs Commentary

On the U.S. Note to Japan 14

— Yan

The U.S. government's note to Japan was delivered to Foreign Minister Hirota yesterday by its ambassador to Tokyo. We carefully examine the wording of the note and the overall position of the U.S. government reflected in it. I feel that the implications are far-reaching. What it involves has actually transcended the simple diplomatic dispute targeting the Japanese side's statement on China, and includes various issues directly related to both Japan and the United States.

For now, let's set aside the content of the note and only observe the fact that it was formally submitted. I feel that it is sufficient to reveal the true face of President Roosevelt's attitude toward Japan in the year since he took office, so that people from all countries with a vital stake in today's Pacific can have a correct understanding in this regard. This is truly a beneficial act. Not only that, but in view of Roosevelt's past silence on the Far East situation, I feel that this sudden epoch-making "frank" statement is even more powerful, and holds the preparation and determination to ultimately implement its claims. Yesterday and the day before, I discussed that Japan would certainly not retract the position it adopted in its statement. This is a strong corroboration. All of our compatriots who feel that Japan has softened because the UK and the U.S. have spoken out fairly and impartially are greatly mistaken. If Japan really softened, the governments of all countries would know it best. Washington's submission of the note is hardly unnecessary.

If we try to put ourselves in Roosevelt's position, we will know that this note to Japan has exhausted the ability to use rhetoric. However, its content is by no means limited to passively protesting Japan. It actually contains an active warning. It is heard that Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota believes that this note is a re-elaboration of the Stimson Doctrine. This can be described as a penetrating comment. The note also mentions the Kellogg-Briand Pact and the treaties signed at the Washington Conference. It also has the phrase "the position of the U.S. government also needs to be re-stated" (according to the Japan United Press translation). The position it refers to is, of course, the position of the Hoover-Stimson administration. The so-called Hoover Doctrine or Stimson Doctrine is a crystallization of this position and contains an active nature. The concrete explanations of this active nature are: (1) The world should not have wars after the Kellogg-Briand Pact was signed. If there is a war, the world will be divided into two major warring groups. There is no so-called neutral party, implying that the U.S. may eventually participate in the war. (2) The situation before the conclusion of the treaties signed at the Washington Conference and the impact after the conclusion all have a chain-like nature. Japan's violation of the Nine-Power Treaty is that even if the U.S. cannot quickly crack down on Japan, it should not expect the U.S. to be bound by the naval treaty forever, implying that the U.S. should use expanding naval power as a means to maintain the balance in the Pacific that has already been destroyed. The original note mentions multilateral treaties between China, Japan, the U.S., and other countries. It uses the word Treaties, which is plural, and it is very clear that it is not limited to the Nine-Power Treaty. From this, it is predicted that Japan and the U.S. will have major disputes at next year's Second Washington Naval Conference to discuss amending the London Naval Treaty, and its conclusions will be the issue of whether the naval ratio between Japan and the U.S. or Japan, the U.S., and the UK should be affected by the changes in the Far East situation after the "September 18th Incident." Hirota is eager to limit the discussion topics to naval disarmament issues at that time, and to exclude the Far East issue, in order to avoid discussing the Sino-Japanese pending issues in the form of an international conference. Roosevelt has taken the opportunity to give a reply rejecting it. I wonder if our country's authorities have made active preparations for this key that has a vital stake.

Furthermore, there are two matters that are related to the submission of this note that are worth noting. One is the tacit agreement between the executive and legislative branches of the U.S. The other is that before the submission, the U.S. State Department had consulted with the UK, France, Italy, and other signatories to the Nine-Power Treaty (of course, excluding Japan). Regarding the former, since Japan's statement was issued, key figures in the Senate, which shares real diplomatic power with the U.S. president, such as Borah, Robinson, and King, have all made public statements, which have greatly influenced public opinion and strengthened Roosevelt's position at home and abroad. Regarding the latter, although this note was submitted unilaterally by the U.S., it has at least received the spiritual support of the authorities of the other seven signatory countries. In our previous article, we said that the time for convening the Nine-Power Treaty Conference has matured. Japan will certainly participate in this conference, which is expected, but our country cannot abandon its treaty rights and obligations. Otherwise, it may not avoid being suspected of violating the treaty itself, let alone others. It must be known that this is the responsibility that all signatory countries should fulfill. There is no so-called pleading for mercy in our country, and there is no so-called showing favor in all countries. This is also a feeling we have gained in addition to paying attention to the U.S. note, and it should be told to our authorities.

Now Roosevelt's attitude toward Japan is very clear. The Soviet Union's preparations for war against Japan are accelerating. The League of Nations' Administrative Council meeting and advisory meeting will be held within half a month to discuss the Far East situation, and the time for next year's Second Washington Naval Conference is also approaching. All of this is closely related to Japan's interests, and the solutions or countermeasures that its national authorities can see are all sought in the rapid oppression of China. It is truly regrettable. Recently, the three-headed meeting of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Hirota, Shigemitsu, and Arima, decided to quickly resolve the Sino-Japanese pending issues through direct negotiations, following the U.S. note, and its military's aggressive strategy has the potential to spread from North China to South China. This shows that the situation is extremely serious. The disaster of national subjugation is imminent for our people. Can they still be at ease and indifferent?

Legislative Yuan Reviews Diplomatic Proposals; Xiao Shuyu's Proposal is Withdrawn at His Own Request; Liu Guantun's Proposal is Passed After Revision 15

(Nanjing) The Review Committee for Diplomatic Proposals of the Legislative Yuan held a review meeting at 3:30 p.m. on the 2nd. Fu Bingchang, Liang Hancao, Liu Guantun, Zhong Tianxin, Gu Zhenggang, Xiao Shuyu, Ma Yinchu, etc. attended. Fu Bingchang chaired. First, Xiao Shuyu's four proposals were reviewed: (1) Sincere unity, (2) Unified construction mechanism, (3) Implement savings to save the country, (4) Nationals should receive military training. After Xiao explained the purpose of the proposals, the committee members all expressed their opinions. All believed that the first point was essential, but it was not within the powers of the Legislative Yuan and was not convenient to propose, so it was decided to retain it. However, Xiao believed that the entire case was related, and if the first point was retained, even if the remaining three points were passed, it would be difficult to take effect. He automatically requested that the entire case be withdrawn. Then, Liu Guantun's diplomatic proposal was reviewed, which included four points: urging the signatory countries of the Nine-Power Treaty to convene a meeting to discuss sanctions against violent Japan, etc. After Liu explained the various points in writing, the proposal was carefully reviewed. As a result, the original text was revised and made into a proposal, which was scheduled to be submitted to the Yuanhui on the 4th for discussion and decision, and then sent to the Central Political Council for the reference of the diplomatic authorities. According to Liang Hancao after the meeting, Xiao's proposal's first two points are outside the scope of legislation and should be expressed by local party departments, etc., or submitted to the central government for review. The result has been deleted. However, Xiao's original intention for the proposal was purely to save the country and had no other intention. As for the Sino-Japanese diplomatic issue, the situation is extremely serious. At this time, the determination of the Nine-Power Treaty must be awakened first. Our country advocates according to law, and all countries should be able to express sympathy. If this is not sought, what else can be sought? Someone said that Japan has now withdrawn the statement it issued on April 10, and the issue has come to an end. This statement is very misleading. We should know that Japan's policy towards China is a long-standing strategic policy. Regardless of whether its statement is withdrawn or not, its policy of aggression against China will never change, or

even be more active. In order to save themselves, the Chinese people should wake up quickly. Diplomacy, in particular, must have a resolute, sensitive, and concrete approach. (2nd Special Telegram)

Broadly Discussing China Policy Between Hirota and Ariyoshi: Direct Negotiations Between the Two Countries to Resolve Outstanding Issues; Rejecting Intervention by the League of Nations and Third Countries; Ariyoshi Clearly Listened to the Military's Intentions Yesterday 16

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota believes that the statement of April 17th achieved the following results: (1) The Japanese people have increased awareness of the importance of the East Asian issue; (2) The British statement on China policy expresses a willingness to advance with mutual understanding with Japan; (3) Japan's determination to oppose all activities to aid China has made this clear to all countries. Therefore, Ariyoshi will be urged to actively negotiate further, in order to reap the actual benefits mentioned above (Xinhua News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota believes that the governments of Britain and the United States have simultaneously understood the purpose of the so-called statement on China policy, and have expressed a friendly attitude. He believes this issue has come to an end, and is very satisfied that Japan's special status has gained the understanding of both Britain and the United States. He has resolved to use this as a background for bravely advancing towards the fundamental resolution of the China issue, and the implementation of peaceful work with Britain and the United States (Dentsu dispatch, 2nd).

(Tokyo) After returning to Tokyo on the 28th, Ambassador to China Akira Ariyoshi immediately visited Foreign Minister Hirota and Vice Minister Shigemitsu at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 3 p.m. The three held a two-hour meeting, focusing on Ambassador Ariyoshi's report and discussing China policy. As a result, the following policies were decided: In the future, a normal channel of Sino-Japanese diplomacy will be established in accordance with these policies, and then efforts will be made to resolve various outstanding issues between China and Japan.

(1) Various issues between China and Japan should be resolved through direct negotiations between the two countries, and intervention by the League of Nations and third countries should not be permitted.

(2) Japan has no intention of invading China. This policy remains unchanged from the past. Japan earnestly hopes for China's unification.

(3) Japan will resolutely repel all means that hinder the normalization of Sino-Japanese relations.

(4) Apart from direct Sino-Japanese negotiations, there is no way to resolve the various outstanding issues between China and Japan, and to adjust the political, economic, and cultural relations between the two countries (Rengo dispatch, 1st).

(Tokyo) Akira Ariyoshi, the Ambassador to China who is currently returning to the country, visited Minister of the Army Hayashi at his official residence yesterday to offer his respects upon returning home. At the same time, he held important talks regarding the recent situation in China, especially the National Government's intentions towards Japan, the situation in South China, and the situations in Xinjiang and Outer Mongolia. He left at 4:30 p.m. Subsequently, Harada Osamu, secretary to Prince Saionji, also visited Minister of the Army Hayashi, reporting that Prince Saionji would be entering Kyoto on the 2nd, and held various important talks. Commander of the Military Police, Qin, visited the Minister of the Army again at 5 p.m. to discuss a major incident and report on recent situations (Dentsu News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

Hiroshi Saito to Return Home Next Month 17

(Tokyo) According to news from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Ambassador to the United States Hiroshi Saito plans to return to Japan in late June for a stay of two months, to report on the progress of all Sino-Japanese negotiations. Saito also hopes to visit Manchuria once to inspect Sino-Japanese relations, and intends to go to Beiping and Nanjing to observe the current situation and exchange opinions with important Chinese figures (Xinhua News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

A Glimpse of the British Press: Japan Attempts to Promote Policies Again, Seeking to Isolate Itself From the World 18

(London) Many British newspapers criticized the statements made by British Foreign Secretary Simon regarding Japan's China policy.

The Times of London stated that, "What may be accepted today is that Japan, when it feels that peace in the Far East is endangered, should not take unilateral action or reject international plans to aid China. This has at least produced the satisfactory result of making world opinion clearly aware of the trend of Japan's policy. Japan's repeated statements about its mission and its obligations and responsibilities for unilateral action naturally raise concerns that Tokyo will expand its influence in the Far East and carry out its policy, which has already been effective in Manchuria. The Japanese government, now aware of the strong public outrage, should know that what is tolerated in the several disintegrated provinces of Northeastern China will not be tolerated if implemented in the South, as the interests of the Chinese central government and other countries will be more affected. If Japan can restore trust after making the same policy statements as other countries, and shift the energy of the Far Eastern countries, which is now spent on preparations to prevent foreign aggression, to construction projects, then much will be gained" (Reuters dispatch, 1st).

Hirota's Irrelevant Answer 19

(London) The Manchester Guardian stated in today's editorial that the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs deeply knows how to remain silent itself while letting its ambassadors speak volubly abroad. What Britain is questioning and what Japan is answering, the gist of which can certainly be found in the statements made by Foreign Secretary Simon in the House of Commons. Foreign Minister Hirota's answer was light and evasive, as expected. The key points inquired by British Ambassador Linley were left unanswered, and he replied with general remarks. Was British Ambassador Linley not asking Japan to explain the statements made by Japanese ambassadors, consuls, and Ministry of Foreign Affairs spokespersons abroad? However, British Foreign Secretary Simon stated that the Japanese reply was still clear, perhaps for strategic reasons. However, we cannot say that the Foreign Secretary is truly satisfied, as the Japanese remarks must be regarded as responsible statements made by responsible personnel with Tokyo's approval. Japan's formal statements and its informal statements clearly contradict each other, but the joint warnings and threats issued by spokespersons from all aspects of Japan cannot be taken lightly. Therefore, this matter has not ended, and we can say that a new page in history has now been opened (Reuters dispatch, 1st).

The Mystery Remains: The Daily Telegraph Reports 20

"The informal declaration issued by the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs on April 17th is surrounded by an unfathomable mystery. Foreign Secretary Simon's declaration yesterday also failed to clarify this mystery. Not only did it not clarify it, but because Japan implicitly withdrew its declaration, and the official explanations that the Tokyo government had previously allowed to be published were indefinitely delayed, this mystery became even more profound and plunged people into a fog. Moreover, the so-called withdrawal is not a correction, and what its official and informal statements declared cannot be said to be non-existent. This is why some people still feel somewhat uneasy. However, this incident has been declared over. Simon, in the midst of the incident, was able to adopt a prudent policy, and with skillful and firm hands, restated Britain's rights. This is to be congratulated for Simon," etc. (Havas dispatch).

Advocating Active Aid to China 21

The Huibao newspaper stated that a strong China is necessary, which is the first essential for peace in the Far East. Western powers should strive to assist Nanjing so that China has the ability to curb unrest (Reuters dispatch).

Gaining a Double Lesson 22

The Morning Post stated, "We hope that from the occurrence of this incident, we can gain a double lesson, that is, for the Western powers, it can make them understand that attempting to isolate Japan is a dangerous thing, and Japan should also know that falling into isolation is also a reckless move," etc. (Havas dispatch).

League of Nations Meeting This Month: Three Major Issues Included on the Agenda; Principle of Non-Recognition of Pseudo-Organizations; Advisory Committee to Conduct Thorough Discussion; All Parties Express Enthusiasm in Welcoming Russia 23

(Geneva) This month, Geneva will discuss important political issues concerning peace in three continents. Those included on the League of Nations' agenda are the Saar plebiscite issue of 1935, the tense situation caused by the Gran Chaco War in South America, and the "Manchukuo" issue in the Far East. Among the three, the Gran Chaco and Saar issues will be discussed at the spring regular meeting of the League of Nations' Administrative Council, which opens on May 14th. The issue of non-recognition of "Manchukuo" will be discussed by the League of Nations' Sino-Japanese Special Advisory Committee, which is convened on the same day. In addition, the disarmament issue will also be raised for discussion. Most politicians on the Administrative Council believe that the fate of the League of Nations depends on whether it can smoothly resolve the disarmament deadlock, and the League of Nations' authority in the United States also depends on its ability to resolve the conflict between Bolivia and Paraguay.

The Sino-Japanese dispute still has repercussions in Geneva. Therefore, when the Sino-Japanese Advisory Committee and the Administrative Council hold meetings at the same time, difficulties will arise. After Britain's request, the Sino-Japanese Advisory Committee scheduled a special meeting to discuss postal relations with Manchuria without violating the League of Nations' principle of non-recognition of "Manchukuo." According to reports, the "Manchukuo" authorities requested that postal fees for mail passing through "Manchukuo" be paid. Britain is deeply concerned that this fact may be mistakenly interpreted as recognition of "Manchukuo" in an invisible way. Therefore, it sought the opinion of the League of Nations Committee. Most well-informed diplomats say that the Sino-Japanese Advisory Committee (of which the United States is also a member) will take the opportunity to conduct a thorough discussion of the principle of non-recognition of "Manchukuo." Since the League of Nations passed the de facto or de jure non-recognition of "Manchukuo," all parties have clearly expressed dissatisfaction with this principle, especially the European and American countries. Britain, France, and Germany have even hinted that the principle hinders business and normal relations with "Manchuria." Therefore, most observers now believe that the committee is inclined to weaken the non-recognition doctrine. Although the League of Nations does not approve of political or commercial relations with "Manchukuo," merchants in France and Germany are now competing for commercial privileges in "Manchukuo." This issue has become increasingly important. Many parties have indicated that the Soviet Union may change its previous attitude of not participating in the Sino-Japanese Advisory Committee. Some diplomats acknowledge that the Soviet Union's participation in this committee will be a prelude to the Soviet Union's joining the League of Nations. European countries are paying special attention to the preparations for the Saar plebiscite and the negotiations on the Franco-German disarmament agreement. The Special Committee on the Saar issue is currently preparing a report for the Administrative Council's discussion. The self-determination of the Saar residents should be held in January 1935. Saar residents who are 20 years old or older and who resided in the area on January 20, 1920, have the right to vote to determine whether the Saar (1) will return to Germany, (2) merge with France, or (3) remain under League of Nations administration. Although this is purely a matter for France and Germany, its resolution is of great importance to the future peace of Europe. German Chancellor Hitler is eager for the Saar to return to Germany and has publicly stated that if the Saar is returned to Germany, Germany and France can live in peace. Therefore, the Administrative Council may encounter fierce debate when discussing this issue. As for the conflict between Bolivia and Paraguay, the League of Nations Special Committee has failed to negotiate a reconciliation in the region. Therefore, the Administrative Council must now devise new solutions for this matter (National Telegram, 2nd).

Four Japanese Warships Arrive in Xiamen; Governor-General of Taiwan Departs to Return to Tokyo 24

(Xiamen) Four Japanese warships arrived in Xiamen on the 2nd (Special dispatch, 2nd).

(Xiamen) Governor-General of Taiwan, Nakagawa, departed from Taipei on the morning of the 2nd to return to Tokyo. He is scheduled to stay for one month before returning, and will issue invitations for the five-territory conference of Fujian, Guangdong, and Shanghai on the other side of the strait (Special dispatch, 2nd).

(Fuzhou) The Nanhua Conference of the Japanese Governor-General's Office in Taiwan decided to hold a grand assembly of overseas Chinese, Fujianese, Japanese, and Taiwanese people on the first day of next month. The proposals will be brought by Japanese Consul Usami Kyo, and the meeting will be held in the Taiwan Public Hall (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Xiamen) Cai Qiao and Cai Bai, who were shot and killed on Xiamen's Shuixian Road, were arrested as major criminals from Wutai. On the 30th, they were extradited by the Japanese consul. Xiang Peizhang, the main culprit and leader of the militia, has surrendered to the Japanese consulate, but the consulate is still keeping it secret (Special dispatch, 2nd).

Japan Requests Consolidation of Old Loans; President of Tokyo Kogyo Company Arrives in Beijing 25

(Nanjing) Diplomatic sources report that Japan suddenly made a request to consolidate old loans. It is reported that Uchida, the president of Tokyo Kogyo Company, has arrived in Beijing from Japan. On the morning of the 2nd, he visited Wang, who is also the Foreign Minister, at the Ministry of Railways' official residence to express his request. The government side stated that our country has long intended to consolidate foreign old loans, but it needs to be discussed at length (Special dispatch, 2nd).

The Pseudo-Regime Divides the Northeast into Twenty-Seven Provinces 26

(Beiping) People from the Northeast say that the pseudo-State Council resolved to change the entire Northeast into twenty-seven provinces, starting on May 1st. At the same time, a conscription system will be started (Special dispatch, 2nd).

The Righteous Act of Overthrowing the Pseudo-Regime Fails; Patriot Gao Chengzhang Apprehended; Plot to Destroy the Pseudo-Capital in Mid-January Failed; Twelve Patriots and a Large Batch of Explosives Seized 27

(Changchun) The Gao Chengzhang conspiracy incident, which aimed to disrupt the "Manchukuo" and obstruct the realization of the imperial system by destroying the main buildings of the four cities of Harbin, Changchun, Shenyang, and Dalian, was brought to light due to the activities of the Harbin Fujiadian Gendarmerie. Party members were identified, explosives were confiscated, and the evil plan was prevented from happening. This plan was suspected of being carried out under the instructions of a certain secret reconnaissance team. In order to investigate, publication was prohibited. It has been four months, and the incident has come to an end. The ban was lifted at 10 a.m. today. The course of the incident is roughly as follows: Fearing that the "Manchukuo Emperor" would ascend the throne, consolidate the national foundation, and that Sino-Japanese relations would become closer, a certain secret reconnaissance team, with team member Gao Chengzhang as the commander, led twelve Chinese people to set off first, carrying fifty explosives disguised as soap, and three boxes of kerosene. In mid-January, they secretly entered Manchuria and began to implement the plan. The party first sent the explosives to Liu Hanlin, a secret agent of the organization in Mudanjiang, and then divided into groups to sneak into the four cities. Just as Harbin was holding the first phase of the grand ceremony's security, Gao Chengzhang, disguised as a coolie, was eventually caught by the gendarmerie. According to his confession, the gendarmerie organized several suicide squads, seized the explosives hidden in Mudanjiang, and the remaining criminals were also arrested by the Japanese and Manchukuo authorities (Dentsu News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

Northeast Righteous Army Attacks Newly Arrived Japanese Troops 28

(Changchun) According to the Kwantung Army, the Tamura Detachment of the Wakayama Unit was attacked by 1,500 members of the Righteous Army near Hengdaohezi at 6:30 a.m. on April 30th. After a fierce battle, the Japanese army suffered seven deaths, including Lieutenant Yoshida, and more than a dozen injuries. Furthermore, at 6 a.m. yesterday, Sergeant Major Imura and sixteen others were escorting sixteen military supply and food carts from Liuhe to Tonghua, when they were suddenly attacked by sixty members of the Righteous Army seven miles northwest of Tonghua. The military supplies and food were all taken away by the Righteous Army, Imura was injured, and the rest of the Japanese army retreated. Upon hearing the news, the Japanese and puppet troops in Tonghua rushed to their aid at 9 a.m., but the shadow of the Righteous Army was no longer to be seen (Xinhua News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Nanjing) According to a special report from Korea, in the past month, Korean newspapers have reported the following situations of the anti-Manchu army in the Northeast: (1) A certain troop of the puppet army stationed in the 24th district of Changbai County suddenly mutinied at noon on April 1st, killing the puppet captain and destroying the Japanese Takemoto Company, and then entered the territory of Fusong County. (2) A certain troop of the Japanese army stationed in Lianshankou fought with more than 150 members of the anti-Manchu army in Wulongbei, south of Wufeijin, on April 6th for several hours. Several Japanese soldiers were injured. Also, a detachment of the Japanese army and the puppet army fought with more than 600 members of the anti-Manchu army near Mishan on April 3rd. Several Japanese soldiers were killed and injured. (3) The Red Spear Anti-Manchu Army, consisting of approximately 300 former subordinates of San Sheng, suddenly attacked Huachuan County on the afternoon of April 8th, but failed due to a small number of people. That night, more than 1,000 reinforcements arrived, and on the morning of the 9th, they occupied the county. At the same time, Tangyuan also fell into danger. Also, the anti-Manchu army led by Ji Wentou attacked the area near the Japanese First Immigrant Village in Yongfeng Town on the 9th. (4) On the evening of April 10th, approximately 50 members of the anti-Manchu army attacked the Liu Dao Hezi Yamamoto Group Construction Office (approximately seven kilometers from Ningguta), killing one Japanese person. (5) The two Korean independent regiments of a certain army had occupied Xingjing County and recently moved to Huanren County and Xiangcao Hezi, sending several subordinates to various places to recruit youths and plan to attack Xingjing County with the anti-Manchu army of Su Ziyu. The subordinate had already snuck three or four hundred members into the vicinity of the county. Moreover, Liang Yu Feng, the commander-in-chief of a certain Korean army, led more than 100 subordinates to wait for an opportunity to take action. The Japanese and puppet military police were extremely alarmed (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

The Eastern Route Army Mobilizes to Pressure Changting; The Southern Route Army Cooperates in Suppressing the Remaining Bandits in Western Fujian; The Aftermath Area of Junmenling Has Been Established; Yikou and Mozhouling Have Both Been Recovered 29

Chiang Orders Fujian and Jiangxi Provincial Governments to Select Talents

To Establish Aftermath Training Classes in Recovered Areas

(Fuzhou) Li Mo'an's division captured Yikou on the 26th, and recovered Mozhouling on the 28th, defeating the pseudo-19th and 34th Divisions. On the 30th, the pseudo-5th Army Corps fled to Taishun. After Sun's division ambushed them from both sides of Meikou and Xiefang, the bandits were defeated. There were captures in each battle. The bandits of Sha Yongzhi were fiercely attacked by the Chen and Lu divisions and are now also retreating. There are no traces of bandits near Xiamu Baimaiyang (Special dispatch, 2nd).

(Hong Kong) The Eastern Route Army telegraphed that it was mobilizing to put pressure on Changting. Wei Lihuang is stationed in Longyan to supervise the army. Chiang Dingwen will also go to the front to inspect (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Hong Kong) Huang Zanbin's division was ordered to surround the remaining bandits in Junmenling and returned to the command of the Second Column (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Hong Kong) The Communist bandits suddenly gathered more than 10,000 troops and were active in western Fujian, plotting to disrupt the rear of the eastern and western routes. Chen Jitang and Chiang Dingwen have ordered various troops to encircle and suppress them (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Hong Kong) Chen Shuying's regiment of the Guangdong Second Division has annihilated the bandits who fled from Dalong (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Hong Kong) The Junmen Aftermath Area has been established, with Huang Yanzhen, Huang Zhiwen, Li Zhenliang, etc. as members. The scope of authority ranges from Xunwu to Panshi Pass and Luotang Tangjiang Chengjiang and other places (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Fuzhou) Chiang Dingwen telegraphed the province to report the recovery of the old counties in western Fujian. In this battle, the bandits of the pseudo-14th Division were attacked from three sides and almost completely wiped out. The Quan Song Xilian Division is now continuing to advance towards western Fujian. The defense of the area will be taken over by the [missing characters] division. Shen Fazao has been appointed to replace Song as the director of the South District Security Sub-Office (Special dispatch, 2nd).

(Hong Kong) Chiang telegraphed Chen Jitang on the 27th to congratulate him on the capture of Junmenling and awarded him 10,000 yuan (Special dispatch, 2nd).

(Nanchang) The pseudo-Xianggan Independent Battalion at the junction of the 48th District of Ji'an surrendered to the 62nd Division of Anfu, bringing with them 274 rifles, 1 machine gun, 10 submachine guns, and 320 personnel. Tao's division sent a battalion to welcome them and held a banquet (Special dispatch, 2nd).

(Nanchang) A dispatch from Ganzhou stated that the Li Zhen Regiment of the First Column defeated the pseudo-Third Army Corps at Yuwengdu, killing hundreds of bandits. Also, the 8th Division attacked Shili Pen Xikeng Wang Dongnan Highland, destroying three bandit fortresses and killing 200 bandits. The remaining bandits retreated to Ruijin and are still advancing towards Xingguo and Huichang (Special dispatch, 2nd).

(Nanchang) Chiang believed that Changting, Qingliu, Liancheng, Ninghua, Jianning, and Ningdu Shicheng, Duanjin, Yudu, Huichang, and Xingguo had either been recovered or would be recovered soon. In order to deal with the aftermath of bandit suppression, there was an urgent need for capable personnel. Therefore, he established Aftermath Training Classes in the recovered counties and districts. On the 29th, he telegraphed the Fujian and Jiangxi provincial governments to select: 1. Those with military and political knowledge and rich bandit suppression experience to be appointed as the magistrates of the above eleven counties; 2. Those who have researched county administration to fill positions as assistants; 3. Virtuous people from the bandit areas who have political experience and are willing to return to their hometowns to serve as clean-up and aftermath cadres (Special dispatch, 2nd).

(Fuzhou) Military sources report that the bandits of the Fifth Army Corps attacked our positions. Our army met them head-on and fiercely attacked them, flanking them from the north of Taining Meikou and Xiefang. The bandits were defeated and lost one-third of their strength. The bandits in Shaxian were continuously attacked by our Chen and Lu divisions and fled backwards. There are now no traces of bandits in Shaxian, Yongan, and Meitai (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Fuzhou) Li Mo'an telegraphed the province from Taining that this division captured Yikou at 4 p.m. on the 26th, and captured the famous strategic pass of Mozhouling on the morning of the 28th. The bandits of the pseudo-19th and 34th Divisions were completely defeated by us. Apart from those killed and captured on the spot, the remaining bandits fled towards [missing characters]. Our army has taken advantage of the victory to advance and suppress them (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd).

(Nanchang) The encirclement and suppression of Fang Zhimin's troops by Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and Anhui are progressing smoothly. Fang's bandits are desperately building bunkers in Hengfeng, trying to resist stubbornly while preventing bandits from escaping to surrender. A certain division obtained information from a pseudo-company commander that the pseudo-army commander Chen Jinlu had already lost an arm in battle. On the 23rd, Fang Zhimin personally supervised the battle at Hengfeng Kengkou and was forced to be wounded in the left arm by artillery fire. All bandit battalion commanders and below want to surrender (Special dispatch, 2nd).

(A) Review of Reports: (1) Interior Minister Huang, Finance Minister Kong, Industry Minister Chen, and Judicial Administration Minister Luo reported on the matter submitted for review by the Ministry of Interior regarding the draft Implementation Law of the Land Law and various supplementary laws, regulations, and attached forms. After holding five meetings, the draft Implementation Law of the Land Law, revised articles, and opinions on the penalty provisions of the law and the chapter on land surveying were formulated. The draft regulations for the organization of land courts, revised articles, and draft regulations for the appointment of assessment commissioners, revised articles, draft regulations for the appointment of deed commissioners, revised articles, and draft arbitration rules, were formulated. Except for the draft regulations for the organization of land courts, revised articles, which will be submitted to the Judicial Yuan for consultation before being presented to the meeting again, the remaining draft regulations, revised articles, will be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review and promulgation if approved. In addition, the implementation law forms and annexes will be sent to the Legislative Yuan for reference. The remaining implementation rules for land surveying will be promulgated by the Executive Yuan after the Implementation Law of the Land Law is promulgated. The arbitration rules, land declaration regulations, land survey regulations, and forms and annexes will be handed over to the Ministry of Interior for further handling after the Implementation Law of the Land Law is promulgated. A request was made for approval of the revised drafts attached. Resolution: Revised and passed, sent to the Legislative Yuan. (2) Interior Minister Huang, Finance Minister, Industry Minister, Education Minister, Communications Minister, Railways Minister, Justice Minister, and Chairman of the Anti-Opium Committee reported on the matter submitted for review regarding how the relationship between the various ministries and commissions and the provincial governments and departments should be clarified in order to increase administrative efficiency. After review, three provisional measures were decided: 1. The various ministries and commissions may directly correspond with the three departments of the various provincial governments, and should still consult the provincial government separately when necessary. 2. If the matter involves more than two departments, in addition to writing to the competent department, the provincial government should still be consulted separately or forwarded by the provincial government. 3. In case of factual need, a request should be submitted to the Executive Yuan to order the provincial government to comply. Resolution: Passed. (3) Interior Minister Huang, Foreign Minister Wang, Communications Minister Zhu, and Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission Chen reported on the matter submitted for review regarding the draft registration measures and registration forms for Overseas Chinese issuing newspapers and magazines submitted by the Ministry of Interior and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. The original proposed measures and attached forms were revised separately, and it is proposed that the Ministry of Interior and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission jointly promulgate and implement them. The registration of overseas party newspapers should still be handled in accordance with the Overseas Party Newspaper Registration Rules promulgated by the Central Executive Committee, and a statement should be made when the promulgation is made. A request was made for instructions on the attached revised drafts and letters. Resolution: Passed according to the review opinions. (4) Interior Minister Huang and Education Minister Wang reported on the matter submitted for review by the Central Government regarding the re-establishment of the National History Museum. After review, four concrete measures were formulated, and a request was made for approval. Resolution: Passed according to the review opinions. (B) Appointments and Dismissals: (1) Resolution: Chen Guofu, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, requested to resign from his concurrent post as Minister of Civil Affairs. (2) The National Government Civil Service Office wrote to the Military Affairs Commission requesting that Yu Feipeng and Xu Tingyao be specially appointed to lead Wei Yifu and others to Europe and the United States to inspect transportation and military affairs. Worldwide Labor Day

Moscow Skies: Over Five Hundred Aircraft Soar; Paris Socialist and Communist Parties Clash; Berlin: Two Million People Attend Grand Gathering; Tokyo: Three Thousand Police Maintain Strict Security 48

(London) According to Reuter's dispatches from various capitals today, fears of disturbances on May Day were unfounded. Paris, Madrid, Havana, New York, and Chicago were the focal points of activity. Paris was under extremely tight guard, resembling a military camp. Machine guns and armored vehicles were prepared for any incident. The radical faction's plan for a general strike to celebrate Labor Day failed. Only workers in the state-run cigarette and match factories went on strike. Of the 30,000 employees of the Paris City Hall, only 400 went on strike, and only 10% of factory workers participated. Police arrested 47 picketers. Socialists and Communists clashed, injuring several people.

The most enthusiastic celebrations worldwide were seen in Germany, but German authorities were also on high alert to prevent any out-of-bounds actions. Berlin initiated a national Labor Day celebration to counteract the Communist celebration. Throughout the country, groups marched to the Danelhof Square to participate in the grand gathering, reaching two million people. When Prussian Premier Goering, in Nazi stormtrooper uniform, ascended the platform, the crowd shouted "Long live Goering!" Military music played, and airplanes soared overhead. When Premier Hitler arrived at the scene, the crowd cheered even more fervently. Hitler, upon taking the stage, stated that today was the first day of Germany's Four-Year Plan. He then spoke of the German people's awakening and the unprecedented developments of the past year, saying that some criticized that Socialism was not yet implemented. He emphasized the importance of their creation. He stated that one thing was undoubtedly clear: bureaucratic politics could not save the country. Hitler also claimed that Germany wanted not revenge but peace. Hitler's speech was filled with patriotism, greatly pleasing the listeners. In Moscow, 160 bombers and 375 reconnaissance and observation aircraft participated in Labor Day, with over 500 aircraft circling the sky, creating an unprecedented air force spectacle in the Russian capital. Millions of civilians marched, holding aloft images of Lenin and Stalin. Another notable feature was a squadron of female soldiers. In London, about 1,800 people, including Communist left-wing groups and the unemployed, held Labor Day in Hyde Park, but the Labor Party and the Trades Union Congress did not participate. Very few representatives from formal unions attended. A dispatch from New Delhi reported that 3,000 textile workers went on strike, causing disturbances and injuring 150 people. The situation in Austria and Spain remained normal. (1st Reuter's dispatch)

Bury: This morning's Labor Day ceremony in the local area, due to the absence of Galen, Commander-in-Chief of the Far Eastern Red Army, featured a speech by the Vice-Chairman of the Far Eastern Military Council. He stated that Japan was vigorously conducting anti-Soviet propaganda in the Far East, and the Red Army should do its utmost to maintain peace in the Far East. However, if imperialists dare to violate the border, they would definitely be met with the most violent strike, and so on. Also, the army participating in the ceremony totaled about 14,000 people, with more than 200 various light and heavy tanks. In addition to the infantry, cavalry, and artillery, the rest were mechanized, and the military appearance was even more orderly than in previous years. (1st Central News Agency dispatch)

(Moscow) Yesterday, on the May Day anniversary, a large-scale military parade was held here. One thousand fighter planes soared in the sky, and more than one hundred thousand citizens participated. Representatives from various embassies attended, including Wu Nan-ru, the acting Chinese ambassador, Feng Sheng-yun, the military attaché, and other embassy staff. (2nd World News Agency dispatch)

(Paris) Yesterday at midnight, a serious riot suddenly broke out in the workers' district. Demonstrators attacked those driving streetcars for business. The drivers called the police, and the demonstrators retreated into buildings in the district, throwing objects at the police and firing guns multiple times, injuring one officer. The police chief, upon hearing the alarm, personally led 2,000 police officers to the scene and, with the assistance of a squadron of patrol troops, surrounded the building. However, all entrances were blocked by rioters. A special police unit is now preparing to charge in wearing helmets. Further reports indicate that at dawn, the rioters, outnumbered, were finally stormed by the police. Some rioters obeyed orders and opened the door, while the rest were subdued by police using gun butts. A total of twenty people were arrested. (2nd Reuter's dispatch)

(Berlin) Today, on Labor Day, an outrageous act occurred in the famous city of Vogelsburg in Bavaria, causing public outrage throughout the country. The Nazi Party had organized a Labor Day celebration and built a wooden enclosure capable of holding ten thousand people, but it was suddenly set on fire. According to eyewitnesses, an explosion was heard before the fire started. The authorities immediately offered a reward of one thousand marks for the capture of the arsonists, promising severe punishment if caught. The Nazi Party leader in Vogelsburg has telegraphed Premier Hitler and Propaganda Minister Goebbels, claiming that the perpetrators were Communists. (1st Reuter's dispatch)

(Tokyo) Today is Labor Day, and various factions from the left and right wings are holding demonstrations in various places. Therefore, three thousand police officers were mobilized and concentrated this morning to prepare for any eventuality. However, the whole day was quiet. Only one left-wing figure, Ms. Inoue, was giving a speech advocating the eradication of Fascism, which is an obstacle to labor, when she was stopped by the police. When right-wingers gathered to demonstrate, they had the following slogans: "Wages should be increased to the standards of the world's top countries," and "Work 48 hours per week." When left-wingers held meetings and demonstrations, their slogans were mostly "Down with Fascism, the enemy of workers and peasants," "Jobs and bread for the unemployed," and "Increase wages by 30%," and so on. (1st Reuter's dispatch)

(New York) Communists in New York celebrated Labor Day today with countless flags, shouting slogans, and holding public speeches and singing the Internationale. The large number of participants was unprecedented. The police had great difficulty maintaining order because they wanted to separate the Communists from the Socialists to prevent clashes between the two parties, which was not easy. The police department announced that it would allow red speeches and the singing of the Internationale on this day, provided there were no riots in principle. Therefore, the marchers became even more enthusiastic. Previously, during Labor Day marches, the police often dispersed the crowd with batons and tear gas. (1st National Telegram)

Bombay: In India, hundreds of people were seriously injured during Labor Day celebrations throughout the country. On the German side, 200 people were injured, and 100 have been hospitalized. (1st National Telegram)

Philippine Assembly Accepts Independence Act: Quezon to Be the First President 49

(Manila) The Philippines has taken its first step towards independence today. At 11:10 this morning, the Senate and House of Representatives held a joint session and unanimously passed the Tydings–McDuffie Act. As a result, the Philippines will become a democratic republic within twelve to thirteen years. Coincidentally, the Philippine Assembly's acceptance of the independence act occurred on the thirty-sixth anniversary of the American naval commander George Dewey's great victory in Manila Bay, when he bloodlessly drove the Spanish out of the Pacific. Senate President Quezon will likely be honored as the first president of the Philippine Republic. Quezon has been involved in the Philippine independence movement for twenty years. He once delivered his famous speech, saying that he would rather live under an independent government, even if it became a hell under Filipino self-rule, than under American rule in paradise. The Tydings–McDuffie Act was passed by the US House of Representatives on March 19 and by the Senate on March 25, allowing the Philippines to become independent within twelve to thirteen years. Previously, the Hare–Hawes–Cutting Act was rejected by the Philippine Senate last year and was withdrawn on January 17. Afterwards, Quezon, the head of the Philippine independence delegation, made a request, which led to this amendment, stipulating that the US Army would withdraw completely within this year, while naval bases would be withdrawn upon the completion of independence. As for the continued establishment of naval fuel matters, the US government and Philippine officials will decide directly. The Philippine Assembly will convene a constitutional convention before October 1 of this year to draft a constitution. (1st National Telegram)

Austria Implements New Constitution: Homeland Security Leader Appointed Deputy Prime Minister 50

Vienna: Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss is currently making every effort to implement the new constitution. Prince Starhemberg, leader of the Austrian Fascist Homeland Security Force, was appointed Deputy Prime Minister today. Former Deputy Prime Minister Fey was appointed National Security Minister, a position similar to the British Cabinet's War Minister. It is widely believed that Prince Starhemberg's appointment as Deputy Prime Minister is a natural result of Austria's transformation into a Fascist state. According to official announcements, President Miklas will sign an agreement between Austria and the Vatican at midnight today, a move that indicates progress in relations between Austria and the Pope in recent months. (1st Reuter's dispatch)

Prussian Premier Goering Resigns: Focuses on Aviation 51

(Berlin) General Goering, Premier of Prussia, submitted his resignation this morning. It is rumored that German Interior Minister Frick will succeed him. It is said that Goering resigned because he is also the German Aviation Commissioner, and serving as both Premier of Prussia hinders his focus on Germany's aviation industry. Therefore, he relinquished the concurrent position to dedicate himself to the affairs of the German Air Force and national defense. After General Goering's resignation, President Hindenburg immediately established a new ministry called the "German Ministry of Science, Education, and Training," with Dr. Rust as the minister. It is said that this change is another step towards concentrating power in accordance with the Nazi Party's plan to reform Germany. (30th Reuter's dispatch)

(Berlin) General Goering's resignation from his concurrent position as Prussian Interior Minister, replaced by German Interior Minister Frick, marks the end of a chapter in Prussian history and another step in the Nazi Party's reform of Germany. As Prussia is the largest state in Germany, its powerful police force will now be under central control, and the right to arrest and imprison criminals throughout the state will also belong to the central government. Of particular importance is that Germany's domestic policy was actually dominated by the Prussian state. Although General Goering will remain the Premier of Prussia, it will be a nominal title without real power. (1st Reuter's dispatch)

Representatives from Sixty Countries: Industrial Property Protection Conference Opens at British Foreign Office Yesterday 52

(London) This morning, representatives from sixty countries gathered in the Locarno Room of the Foreign Office. The Minister of Commerce, Runciman, presided over the opening ceremony of the International Conference for the Protection of Industrial Property. Runciman first read a letter from the British monarch, expressing welcome and goodwill to the representatives. Then, he declared that the purpose of the conference was to discuss the latest instruments for managing international industrial property rights. At a time when export trade is crucial, the independence of trademarks, the preservation of patent rights, and other issues are known to be important. The British chief representative, Ross, was elected chairman of the conference. The proceedings will be conducted in private. (2nd Reuter's dispatch)

Ping-Guangzhou Air Route Officially Begins: First Flight Completed 53

(Hong Kong) The Ping-Guangzhou route officially opened on the 1st. The plane took off from Guangzhou at 7 am, carrying 2444 cubic centimeters of mail. It arrived in Changsha at 10 am, Wuhan at noon, and could reach Luoyang at 4:10 pm. (1st Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The plane on the Eurasia Aviation Corporation's Ping-Guangzhou line, flying from Guangzhou to Beiping, arrived here from Taiyuan at 2:15 pm today. The plane carried four company employees and some mail. (2nd Reuter's dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Ping-Guangzhou line officially launched on the 1st. At 7 am, the company dispatched three German pilots, engineers, and radio operators from Baiyun Airport, without passengers or mail. (1st Central News Agency dispatch)

(Beiping) The Eurasia Company's Ping-Guangzhou line began operation on the 1st. At 8 am, pilot Lehn flew Eurasia aircraft No. 7 from Nanyuan, carrying three passengers and four large bags of mail. It passed through Bingding and Shantou at noon and was expected to arrive in Luoyang at 2 pm. Because the three passengers were going to Gansu, they would transfer to the Shanghai-Xinjiang plane in Luoyang to fly to Lanzhou. The Ping-Guangzhou plane would stop overnight in Luoyang. It would depart from Luoyang at 9 am on the 2nd, pass through Hankou and Changsha, and go straight to Guangzhou. From then on, there would be round-trip flights between Ping-Guangzhou every Tuesday and Thursday. The company originally planned to hold a launch ceremony this morning and invite people from all walks of life, but it was canceled due to the rush of time. Only commemorative postmarks were added to the letters to commemorate the event. (1st Central News Agency dispatch)

(Guangzhou) The first flight of the Ping-Guangzhou line was completed this afternoon. Eurasia Aviation's No. 1 plane, piloted by German pilot Köster, safely arrived here from Changsha at 6:40 pm. The plane carried no passengers, only some mail. It took four hours to fly from Changsha to here and less than five hours from Wuhan to Guangzhou. According to Köster speaking to a Reuter's reporter, except for the section from Hankou to Changsha, where the weather was bad, the entire journey was exceptionally smooth. The plane is scheduled to fly back to Beiping tomorrow morning. (2nd Reuter's dispatch)

(Hankou) The Eurasia Aviation Ping-Guangzhou line officially opened on the 1st. It took off from Guangzhou City in the morning and arrived in Hankou at 12 noon. It stopped for 20 minutes before flying to Beiping. The plane from Beiping to Guangzhou is scheduled to arrive in Hankou at 12:25 pm on the 2nd. (1st Special Dispatch)

British Merchants Interested in Investing in Huai River Diversion Project: Huai River Diversion Committee in Preliminary Talks 56

(Nanjing) The Huai River Diversion Committee is facing considerable financial difficulties. Recently, a British foreign firm has proposed to invest in the committee, with a substantial amount, and is willing to use the profits obtained from the Huai River diversion into the Yangtze River as collateral. This is because after the completion of the Huai River diversion into the Yangtze River project, the two lakes of Gaoyou and Baoying alone will reveal 8 million mu of fertile land. The authorities of the committee believe that the Huai River diversion project cannot be stopped, and the allocation of the Boxer Indemnity is too slow to meet the urgent need. They have begun preliminary talks with the foreign firm. Whether they can accept the investment in the future depends on the decision of the central government. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Salt Field Land Tax Proposed to Be Included in Provincial Tax Revenue 58

(Nanjing) The salt field land tax in the Lianghuai, Liangzhe, and Changlu areas has always been collected by the Salt Affairs Administration. This income accounts for three-tenths of the Salt Affairs Administration's revenue. The Ministry of Finance believes that the various exorbitant taxes and levies in the provinces must be abolished, and reductions in land tax surcharges must also be supported. Although the detailed measures are subject to the decision of the National Fiscal Administration Conference, the provinces must not use the abolition of miscellaneous taxes and the reduction of surcharges as an excuse to affect local revenue. It is now proposed that the salt field land tax, which has always been a central revenue, be changed to a provincial tax revenue to offset the reduction of surcharges and the abolition of exorbitant taxes and levies. The Ministry of Finance is currently drafting the details so that they can be submitted to the National Finance Conference for discussion. (2nd Special Dispatch)

National Farmer Survey: 31% Increase in Sixty Years 68

(Nanjing) The Central Agricultural Experiment Station of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce recently conducted an on-site survey of 22 provinces by more than 6,000 agricultural information reporters. It is estimated that the national rural population has increased by 31% in the past sixty years, averaging slightly more than 0.5% per year. Except for the five provinces of Ningxia, Shaanxi, Gansu, Jiangxi, and Fujian, where the population has decreased slightly due to natural disasters and banditry, most provinces have seen increases without decreases. (2nd Central News Agency dispatch)

Yuehan Railway: Results of Drilling at the Location of the Lu River Bridge 69

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways believes that the issue of the location of the Lu River Bridge on the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section of the Yuehan Railway has been delayed for a long time. Currently, the Yuehan Railway urgently needs to be completed. The Hunan-Hubei Railway Bureau has been ordered to conduct drilling at the riverbed of the two bridge locations. Although the upstream line is 18 meters shorter in river width, the cost can be slightly reduced from the perspective of the bridge itself. The downstream line is 600 meters shorter, and the dam road padding is not as high or deep as the upstream. In terms of track laying, earthwork, drainage construction, and land acquisition, there will be more savings. Moreover, there are four fewer large and small culverts. The downstream line can save approximately 150,000 yuan in construction costs. The route is straighter, facilitating vehicle movement, and reducing road maintenance costs. The Ministry of Railways has ordered rapid construction to ensure early completion. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Key Points of the Method for Issuing Bonds for the Yuehan Railway 72

(Nanjing) The main points for issuing bonds for the Yuehan Railway project: (1) Total amount: £1.5 million in British currency; (2) Purpose: Completion of the Yuehan Railway and supplementation of construction funds; (3) Annual interest rate: 6%; (4) Repayment period: 13 years; (5) Security: Boxer Indemnity funds borrowed by the Ministry of Railways from the British; (6) The ministries of Finance, Railways, and Industry, along with the Boxer Indemnity Committee, will jointly form a fund management committee. (2nd Special Dispatch)

Reasons for Shelving the Withdrawal of Salt Certificates 73

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance proposed withdrawing the salt certificates of Lianghuai at the Salt Affairs Conference. After Lianghuai Salt Transport Envoy Miao Qiujie proposed a method for withdrawing them over eight years, the principle was approved. The Ministry of Finance was to study the steps and implement them separately. The reasons why the Ministry of Finance decided to shelve the case were: (1) The loans of merchants in Lianghuai cannot be repaid temporarily; (2) After the salt certificate system is abolished, the equipment for on-site tax collection is insufficient, and it is difficult to collect all taxes. (2nd Special Dispatch)

International Commercial Telegraph

—May 2nd Reuters Special Commercial News—Gold and Silver 90

London Gold Price: The London gold price this morning was 136 shillings and 3.5 pence, up 4 pence.

London Silver: The London silver market was firm today. The spot price was quoted at 18 pence and 6875, up half a penny; the futures price was 18 pence and 8125, up 5625. China and the United States were buying, and India was selling. The closing market was uncertain.

American Silver: The New York silver market opened today (May 2nd) steady due to foreign telegraphs. Market participants seemed to be waiting for developments in Washington, and sentiment was good, as it was expected that the May buying trend of the past few days might resume. However, the market remained sluggish, with prices similar to London. Although there was talk that Senator Thomas might introduce a new silver amendment in the Senate, the silver market did not feel the impact of this. The opening prices for forward contracts were down 1 to 25 pounds compared to yesterday's closing prices, except for July, which was up three pounds.

Indian Silver: The Mumbai silver market was steady today. The spot price was 51 rupees and 10 annas, up 14 annas. Both the May and June contracts were up 13 annas.

Special Telegram: He Sheng Foreign Firm received a special telegram from London stating that the London Financial Times editorial first stated that the recent sharp drop in silver prices was mostly due to the United States' silver situation. It then stated that without a real improvement in the financial situation in India and China, it is impossible for silver prices to rise. Only after China and India prosper and recover will they have the power to purchase silver. The previous high silver prices only made China and India tend to sell silver, and needlessly increased the Chinese exchange rate, hindering trade, and delaying the real upward trend of silver.

Exchange Rates 91

British-American: The London foreign exchange market this morning (May 2nd) saw the pound weaken due to US purchases. The opening price for the British-American exchange rate was 5 dollars, 1 dime and 75, down half a cent compared to yesterday's closing price. At 11 AM, it rose 375 to 5 dollars, 1 dime, 1 cent and 125, but at noon, it fell 4375 again to 5 dollars, 1 dime and 6875. At 1 PM in the afternoon, the price was 5 dollars, 1 dime and 5625, down 125. At 2 PM, it returned to 5 dollars, 1 dime and 75. At 3 PM, it rose 3125 again to 5 dollars, 1 dime, 1 cent and 625. Also, one US dollar equals three shillings, ten pence and 961 British pence.

British-French: The opening price was 77 francs and 06, down 12 pounds compared to yesterday's closing price. At 11 AM, it rose 9 pounds to 77 francs and 15, but at noon, it fell to 77 francs and 09. There was no change at 1 PM and 2 PM in the afternoon. At 3 PM, it rose 6 pounds to 77 francs and 15.

American-British: The opening price for the New York exchange rate against the British pound today was 5.11.0, down 25 from the previous day's closing price. At 234, the market did not move. At 56, the market recovered 25, changing to 5.11.25.

American-French: The opening price for the New York exchange rate against the French franc today was 6.62.50, down 0.5 from the previous day.

Cotton and Wheat 92

American Cotton: Although the opening sentiment in the cotton market was low, the price rose due to replenishment from Bank Street and purchases from allied Liverpool and the Far East, absorbing retail selling and local New Orleans and spot traders. Following telegrams from Liverpool, cotton prices continued to rise.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market price for the July contract was 5.66, up 8 pounds from yesterday.

Liverpool Wheat: The wheat market price for the July contract was 4 shillings, 3 pence and 875, the same as yesterday's price.

Indian Cotton: In the Mumbai cotton market today, European exporters sold the July contract and bought 1935 new white Broach cotton, but speculators bought large quantities of the July contract. The July-August Broach cotton price was 188 rupees and 25, up 5 rupees and 25.

Rubber 93

New York: The rubber market showed sympathy with London, remaining active and firm. Profit-taking was offset by general strong demand, but prices were still lower than London. Sentiment remained bullish.

London: The rubber market was firm today. At noon, the transaction prices for the July and September contracts were 7 pence and 125, up 25 from yesterday's closing price.

Securities 94

New York: The stock market opened firm today (May 2nd). The actual position has improved, but external news and the instability of major commodities make people cautious. There are few signs of recovery in the market. Some stocks that rose at the opening slightly expanded. However, American Telephone stock continued to be weak, with the price falling by one pound, which is a cause for concern.
